<p><b>LinkedIn</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ŋ/ 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a business and employment-oriented <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social networking service</a> that operates via <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">websites</a>. Founded on December 28, 2002,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and launched on May 5, 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-7">[7]</a></sup> it is mainly used for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_network" title="Professional network">professional networking</a>, including employers posting jobs and job seekers posting their <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_vitae" title="Curriculum vitae">CVs</a>. As of 2015, most of the site's revenue came from <a href="/wiki/Sales" title="Sales">selling</a> access to <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a> about its users to recruiters and sales professionals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> As of September 2016, LinkedIn has more than 467 million accounts, out of which more than <a href="/wiki/List_of_virtual_communities_with_more_than_100_million_active_users" title="List of virtual communities with more than 100 million active users">106 million are active</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-num_users_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-num_users-5">[5]</a></sup> LinkedIn allows users (workers and employers) to create <a href="/wiki/User_profile" title="User profile">profiles</a> and "connections" to each other in an <a href="/wiki/Online_and_offline" title="Online and offline">online</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_network" title="Social network">social network</a> which may represent real-world <a href="/wiki/Business_relations" title="Business relations">professional relationships</a>. Users can invite anyone (whether a site user or not) to become a connection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Help.linkedin.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Help.linkedin.com-9">[9]</a></sup> The "gated-access approach" (where contact with any professional requires either an existing relationship, or the intervention of a contact of theirs) is intended to build trust among the service's users. LinkedIn participated in the EU's <a href="/wiki/International_Safe_Harbor_Privacy_Principles" title="International Safe Harbor Privacy Principles">International Safe Harbor Privacy Principles</a>.</p>
<p>The site has an <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a> ranking as the 14th most popular website (October 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alexa_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-alexa-4">[4]</a></sup> According to the <i>New York Times</i>, US high school students are now creating LinkedIn profiles to include with their college applications. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Based in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_the_United_States" title="List of companies of the United States">United States</a>, the site is, as of 2013, available in 24 languages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> LinkedIn filed for an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in January 2011 and traded its first shares on May 19, 2011, under the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a> <a href="/wiki/Ticker_symbol" title="Ticker symbol">symbol</a> "LNKD".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 13, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> announced plans to acquire LinkedIn for $26.2 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news_Micr_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-news_Micr-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj_ms_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_ms-16">[16]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on December 8, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The transaction resulted in the payment of approximately $26.4 billion in cash merger consideration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_overview">Company overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Company overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3792" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg/220px-LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg/330px-LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg/440px-LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LinkedIn_Headquarters_Mountain_View.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former LinkedIn headquarters on Stierlin Court in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, CA</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>LinkedIn is <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">headquartered</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California#Economy" title="Sunnyvale, California">Sunnyvale, California</a>, with offices in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Omaha,_Nebraska#Telecommunications_and_information_technology" title="Economy of Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Chicago" title="Economy of Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles#Economy" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_York_(state)" title="Economy of New York (state)">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco#Economy" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Washington_(state)" title="Economy of Washington (state)">Washington</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sao_Paulo" title="Economy of Sao Paulo">Sao Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_London" title="Economy of London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Dublin#ICT_Sector" title="Economy of Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam#Economy" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Milan" title="Economy of Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Paris" title="Economy of Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich#Economy" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Madrid" title="Economy of Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm#Economy" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Singapore" title="Economy of Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hong_Kong" title="Economy of Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_China" title="Economy of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Australia" title="Economy of Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Canada" title="Economy of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Dubai" title="Economy of Dubai">Dubai</a>. In January 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">company</a> had around 9,200 <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">employees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfbusiness_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-sfbusiness-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>LinkedIn's <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> is <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Weiner" title="Jeff Weiner">Jeff Weiner</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup> previously a <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo! Inc.</a> executive. Founder <a href="/wiki/Reid_Hoffman" title="Reid Hoffman">Reid Hoffman</a>, previously CEO of LinkedIn, is Chairman of the Board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> It is funded by <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_Capital" title="Sequoia Capital">Sequoia Capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greylock_Partners" title="Greylock Partners">Greylock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bain_Capital_Ventures" title="Bain Capital Ventures">Bain Capital Ventures</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bessemer_Venture_Partners" title="Bessemer Venture Partners">Bessemer Venture Partners</a> and the European Founders Fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> LinkedIn reached profitability in March 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Through January 2011, the company had received a total of $103 million of <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">investment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPO_rumour_Jan_2011_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPO_rumour_Jan_2011-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_LinkedIn" title="Timeline of LinkedIn">Timeline of LinkedIn</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_to_2010">Founding to 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Founding to 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company was founded in December 2002 by <a href="/wiki/Reid_Hoffman" title="Reid Hoffman">Reid Hoffman</a> and founding team members from <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> and Socialnet.com (Allen Blue, Eric Ly, Jean-Luc Vaillant, Lee Hower, Konstantin Guericke, Stephen Beitzel, David Eves, Ian McNish, Yan Pujante, Chris Saccheri).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In late 2003, <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_Capital" title="Sequoia Capital">Sequoia Capital</a> led the <a href="/wiki/Series_A_round" title="Series A round">Series A</a> investment in the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In August 2004, LinkedIn reached 1 million users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byers2013_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Byers2013-26">[26]</a></sup> In March 2006, LinkedIn achieved its first month of profitability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byers2013_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Byers2013-26">[26]</a></sup> In April 2007, LinkedIn reached 10 million users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byers2013_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Byers2013-26">[26]</a></sup> In February 2008, LinkedIn launched a mobile version of the site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MyUser_Https:_September_11_2016c_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-MyUser_Https:_September_11_2016c-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2008, Sequoia Capital, Greylock Partners, and other <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> firms purchased a 5% <a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">stake</a> in the company for $53 million, giving the company a <a href="/wiki/Post-money_valuation" title="Post-money valuation">post-money valuation</a> of approximately $1 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In 2006, LinkedIn reached 20 million members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2010, LinkedIn opened an International Headquarters in Dublin, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland#Information_and_communications_technology" title="Economy of the Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> received a $20 million investment from <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Management" title="Tiger Management">Tiger Global Management LLC</a> at a valuation of approximately $2 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and announced its first acquisition, Mspoke,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and improved its 1% <a href="/wiki/Premium_(marketing)" title="Premium (marketing)">premium</a> <a href="/wiki/Subscription_business_model" title="Subscription business model">subscription</a> ratio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In October of that year Silicon Valley Insider ranked the company No. 10 on its Top 100 List of most valuable start ups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> By December, the company was valued at $1.575 billion in private markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_to_present">2011 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2011 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:222secondStreet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/222secondStreet.jpg/220px-222secondStreet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/222secondStreet.jpg/330px-222secondStreet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/222secondStreet.jpg/440px-222secondStreet.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:222secondStreet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
LinkedIn office building at <a href="/wiki/222_Second_Street" title="222 Second Street">222 Second Street</a> in San Francisco (opened in March 2016)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg/220px-LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg/330px-LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg/440px-LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LinkedInOfficeToronto2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
LinkedIn Office in Toronto.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>LinkedIn filed for an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in January 2011. The company traded its first shares on May 19, 2011, under the NYSE symbol "LNKD", at $45 per share. Shares of LinkedIn rose as much as 171 percent in their first day of trade on the New York Stock Exchange and closed at $94.25, more than 109 percent above <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">IPO</a> price. Shortly after the IPO, the site's underlying <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/infrastructure#Noun" title="wikt:infrastructure">infrastructure</a> was revised to allow accelerated revision-release cycles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2011, LinkedIn earned $154.6 million in <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a> revenue alone, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, which earned $139.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> LinkedIn's fourth-<a href="/wiki/Quarterly_finance_report" title="Quarterly finance report">quarter</a> 2011 earnings soared because of the company's increase in success in the social media world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> By this point, LinkedIn had about 2,100 full-time employees compared to the 500 that it had in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Q2 2012, LinkedIn leased 57,120 square feet on three floors of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_Montgomery_Tower" title="One Montgomery Tower">One Montgomery Tower</a> building in the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_San_Francisco" title="Financial District, San Francisco">Financial District of San Francisco</a>, which was expanded to 135,000 square feet by 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-40">[40]</a></sup> In May 2012, LinkedIn announced its 2012 Q1 revenues were up to $188.5 million compared to $93.9 million in Q1 2011. Net income increased 140% over Q1 2011 to $5 million. Revenue for Q2 was estimated to be between $210 to $215 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In November 2012, LinkedIn released their third quarter earnings, reporting <a href="/wiki/Earnings_per_share" title="Earnings per share">earnings-per-share</a> of $0.22 on revenue of $252 million. As a result of these numbers, LinkedIn's <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> increased in <a href="/wiki/Valuation_(finance)" title="Valuation (finance)">value</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_(financial_instrument)" title="Trade (financial instrument)">trading</a> at roughly $112 a share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mashable.com_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-mashable.com-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, LinkedIn announced that it had leased <a href="/wiki/222_Second_Street" title="222 Second Street">222 Second Street</a>, a 26-story building under construction in <a href="/wiki/South_of_Market,_San_Francisco" title="South of Market, San Francisco">San Francisco's SoMa</a> district, to accommodate up to 2,500 of its employees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-40">[40]</a></sup> with the lease covering 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfbusiness_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-sfbusiness-2">[2]</a></sup> The goal was to join all San Francisco based staff (1,250 as of January 2016) in one building, bringing sales and <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">marketing</a> employees together with the <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfbusiness_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-sfbusiness-2">[2]</a></sup> They started to move in in March 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfbusiness_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-sfbusiness-2">[2]</a></sup> In February 2016, following an <a href="/wiki/Earnings" title="Earnings">earnings</a> report, LinkedIn's shares dropped 43.6% within a single day, down to $108.38 per share. LinkedIn lost $10 billion of its <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On June 13, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> announced it would acquire LinkedIn for $196 a share, a total value of $26.2 billion and the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Microsoft" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Microsoft">acquisition made by Microsoft</a> to date. The acquisition will be an all-cash, debt-financed transaction. Microsoft will allow LinkedIn to "retain its distinct brand, culture and independence", with Weiner to remain as CEO, who will then report to Microsoft CEO <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a>. Analysts believe Microsoft saw the opportunity to integrate LinkedIn with its <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Office product suite</a> to help better integrate the professional network system with its <a href="/wiki/Product_(business)" title="Product (business)">products</a>. The deal was completed on 12/08/2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wsj_ms_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_ms-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its headquarters in Dublin it currently has 1000 employees. It is expected to increase with the announcement of 200 new jobs taking the total employees to 1200<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2012, LinkedIn acquired 15 key <a href="/wiki/Digg" title="Digg">Digg</a> <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> for $4 million including a "<a href="/wiki/Like_button" title="Like button">click a button to vote up a story</a>" patent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit">Lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, a <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">lawsuit</a> was filed against the company, accusing it of automatically sending invitations to contacts in a user's <a href="/wiki/Email_address" title="Email address">email address</a> book without permission. The court agreed with LinkedIn that permission had in fact been given for invitations to be sent, but <i>not</i> for the two further reminder <a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">emails</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> LinkedIn settled the lawsuit in 2015 for $13 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>This lawsuit was called <i>Perkins vs. LinkedIn Corp .</i> Many users should have got a notice in their e-mail that said Legal Notice of Settlement of Class Action as the subject line in the e-mail. The Case No.13-CV-04303-LHK .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2502" data-file-width="3503" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg/200px-Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg/300px-Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg/400px-Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linkedin_Chocolates.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Social media websites can also use "traditional" marketing approaches, as seen in these LinkedIn-branded chocolates.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2015, LinkedIn had more than 400 million members in over 200 countries and territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-in_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-in-71">[71]</a></sup> It is significantly ahead of its competitors <a href="/wiki/Viadeo" title="Viadeo">Viadeo</a> (50 million as of 2013)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thenextweb_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-thenextweb-72">[72]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/XING" title="XING">XING</a> (11 million as of 2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In 2011, its membership grew by approximately two new members every second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoMembersASecond_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-TwoMembersASecond-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="User_profile_network">User profile network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: User profile network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The basic functionality of LinkedIn allows users (workers and employers) to create <a href="/wiki/User_profile" title="User profile">profiles</a>, which for employees typically consist of a <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_vitae" title="Curriculum vitae">curriculum vitae</a> describing their work experience, education and training and a photo of them. Users can list their workplace skills on their profile. As well, the site enables users to make "connections" to each other in an <a href="/wiki/Online_and_offline" title="Online and offline">online</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_network" title="Social network">social network</a> which may represent real-world <a href="/wiki/Business_relations" title="Business relations">professional relationships</a>. Users can invite anyone (whether a site user or not) to become a connection. However, if the invitee selects "I don't know" or "<a href="/wiki/Spamming" title="Spamming">Spam</a>", this counts against the inviter. If the inviter gets too many of such responses, the <a href="/wiki/User_(computing)" title="User (computing)">user's account</a> may be <a href="/wiki/Block_(Internet)" title="Block (Internet)">restricted or closed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Help.linkedin.com_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Help.linkedin.com-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>This list of connections can then be used in a number of ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtaining introductions to the connections of connections (termed <i>second-degree connections</i>) and connections of second-degree connections (termed <i>third-degree connections</i>)</li>
<li>Users can search for second-degree connections who work at a specific company they are interested in, and then ask a specific first-degree connection in common for an introduction<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SecondDegreeConnections_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-SecondDegreeConnections-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li>Users can <a href="/wiki/Job_hunting" title="Job hunting">find jobs</a>, people and business opportunities recommended by someone in one's contact network.</li>
<li>Employers can list <a href="/wiki/Job" title="Job">jobs</a> and search for potential candidates.</li>
<li>Job seekers can review the profile of hiring managers and discover which of their existing contacts can introduce them.</li>
<li>Users can post their own photos and view photos of others to aid in identification.</li>
<li>Users can follow different companies.</li>
<li>Users can save (i.e. bookmark) jobs that they would like to <a href="/wiki/Application_for_employment" title="Application for employment">apply</a> for.</li>
<li>Users can "like" and "congratulate" each other's updates and new employments.</li>
<li>Users can wish each other a happy birthday.</li>
<li>Users can see who has visited their profile page.</li>
</ul>
<p>The "gated-access approach" (where contact with any professional requires either an existing relationship, or the intervention of a contact of theirs) is intended to build trust among the service's users. LinkedIn participated in the EU's <a href="/wiki/International_Safe_Harbor_Privacy_Principles" title="International Safe Harbor Privacy Principles">International Safe Harbor Privacy Principles</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_and_technology">Security and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Security and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2012, <a href="/wiki/Cryptographic_hash_function" title="Cryptographic hash function">cryptographic hashes</a> of approximately 6.4 million LinkedIn user <a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">passwords</a> were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_crime" title="Computer crime">stolen</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hacker_(computer_security)" title="Hacker (computer security)">hackers</a> who then published the stolen hashes online.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> This action is known as the <a href="/wiki/2012_LinkedIn_hack" title="2012 LinkedIn hack">2012 LinkedIn hack</a>. In response to the incident, LinkedIn asked its users to change their passwords. <a href="/wiki/White_hat_(computer_security)" title="White hat (computer security)">Security experts</a> criticized LinkedIn for not <a href="/wiki/Salt_(cryptography)" title="Salt (cryptography)">salting</a> their password file and for using a single iteration of <a href="/wiki/SHA-1" title="SHA-1">SHA-1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On May 31, 2013 LinkedIn added <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two-factor_authentication" title="Two-factor authentication">two-factor authentication</a>, an important <a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">security</a> enhancement for preventing hackers from gaining access to accounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In May 2016, 117 million LinkedIn usernames and passwords were offered for sale online for the equivalent of $2,200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> These account details are believed to be sourced from the original 2012 LinkedIn hack, in which the number of user IDs stolen had been underestimated. To handle the large volume of emails sent to its users every day with notifications for messages, profile views, important happenings in their network, and other things, LinkedIn uses the Momentum email platform from Message Systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LinkedIn 'applications' often refers to external third party applications that interact with LinkedIn's developer API. However, in some cases it could refer to sanctioned applications featured on a user's profile page.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="External.2C_Third_Party_Applications">External, Third Party Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: External, Third Party Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On February 12, 2015 LinkedIn released an updated terms of use for their developer API.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The developer API allows both companies and individuals the ability to interact with LinkedIn's data through creation of managed third party applications. Applications must go through a review process and request permission from the user before accessing a user's data.</p>
<p>Normal use of the API is outlined in <a class="external text" href="https://developer.linkedin.com/" rel="nofollow">LinkedIn's developer documents</a>, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sign in to external services using LinkedIn</li>
<li>Add items or attributes to a user profile</li>
<li>Share items or articles to user's timeline</li>
</ul>
<p>On a more rare occasion, applications have been developed by third parties to extend LinkedIn's native functions. For instance, LinkedIn does not allow users to define images that correlate with articles or links they share, but this can be done using a third party application like <a class="external text" href="http://www.datopstech.com/linkedin-share-tool/" rel="nofollow">LinkedIn Advanced Share</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_in_Profile">Embedded in Profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Embedded in Profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In October 2008, LinkedIn enabled an "applications platform" which allows external online services to be embedded within a member's profile page. Among the initial applications were an <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> Reading List that allows LinkedIn members to display books they are reading, a connection to Tripit, and a <a href="/wiki/Six_Apart" title="Six Apart">Six Apart</a>, <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a> and <a href="/wiki/TypePad" title="TypePad">TypePad</a> application that allows members to display their latest blog postings within their LinkedIn profile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In November 2010, LinkedIn allowed businesses to list products and services on company profile pages; it also permitted LinkedIn members to "recommend" products and services and write reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after, some of the external services are no longer supported, including Amazon's Reading List <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile">Mobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A mobile version of the site was launched in February 2008, which gives access to a reduced feature set over a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a>. The mobile service is available in six languages: Chinese, English, French, German, Japanese and Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> In January 2011, LinkedIn acquired CardMunch, a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a> maker that scans <a href="/wiki/Business_card" title="Business card">business cards</a> and converts into contacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In June 2013, CardMunch was noted as an available LinkedIn app.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hempel2013_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-hempel2013-11">[11]</a></sup> In August 2011, LinkedIn revamped its mobile applications on the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>. At the time, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Web" title="Mobile Web">mobile page</a> views of the application were increasing roughly 400% year over year according to CEO Jeff Weiner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In October 2013, LinkedIn announced a service for iPhone users called "Intro", which inserts a thumbnail of a person's LinkedIn profile in correspondence with that person when reading mail messages in the native iOS <a href="/wiki/Mail_(Apple)" title="Mail (Apple)">Mail program</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> This is accomplished by re-routing all emails from and to the iPhone through LinkedIn <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>, which security firm Bishop Fox asserts has serious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privacy_issues_of_social_networking_sites" title="Privacy issues of social networking sites">privacy implications</a>, violates many organizations' <a href="/wiki/Security_policy" title="Security policy">security policies</a>, and resembles a <a href="/wiki/Man-in-the-middle_attack" title="Man-in-the-middle attack">man-in-the-middle attack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Groups">Groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LinkedIn also supports the formation of interest groups, and as of March 29, 2012 there are 1,248,019 such groups whose membership varies from 1 to 744,662.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The majority of the largest groups are employment related, although a very wide range of topics are covered mainly around professional and career issues, and there are currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> 128,000 groups for both academic and corporate alumni.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Groups support a limited form of discussion area, moderated by the group owners and managers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Since groups offer the functionality to reach a wide audience without so easily falling foul of <a href="/wiki/Anti-spam_techniques" title="Anti-spam techniques">anti-spam solutions</a>, there is a constant stream of spam postings, and there now exist a range of firms who offer a spamming service for this very purpose. LinkedIn has devised a few mechanisms to reduce the volume of spam,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> but recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> took the decision to remove the ability of group owners to inspect the email address of new members in order to determine if they were spammers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Groups also keep their members informed through emails with updates to the group, including most talked about discussions within your professional circles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Groups may be private, accessible to members only or may be open to Internet users in general to read, though they must join in order to post messages.</p>
<p>In December 2011, LinkedIn announced that they are rolling out polls to groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In November 2013, LinkedIn announced the addition of Showcase Pages to the platform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2014, LinkedIn announced they were going to be removing Product and Services Pages<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> paving the way for a greater focus on Showcase Pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Job_listings">Job listings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Job listings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LinkedIn allows users to research companies, non-profit organizations, and governments they may be interested in working for. Typing the name of a company or organization in the search box causes pop-up data about the company or organization to appear. Such data may include the ratio of female to male employees, the percentage of the most common titles/positions held within the company, the location of the company's headquarters and offices, and a list of present and former employees. In July 2011, LinkedIn launched a new feature allowing companies to include an "Apply with LinkedIn" button on job listing pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plugin_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plugin-100">[100]</a></sup> The new plugin allowed potential employees to apply for positions using their LinkedIn profiles as resumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plugin_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Plugin-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_recruiting">Online recruiting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Online recruiting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Job recruiters, head hunters, and personnel HR are increasingly using LinkedIn as a source for finding potential candidates. By using the Advanced search tools, recruiters can find members matching their specific key words with a click of a button. They then can reach out to those members by sending a request to connect or by sending InMail about a specific job opportunity he or she may have. Recruiters also often join industry based groups on LinkedIn to create connections with professionals in that line of business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skills">Skills</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Skills">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since September 2012, LinkedIn has enabled users to "endorse" each other's skills. This feature also allows users to efficiently provide commentary on other users profiles – network building is reinforced. However, there is no way of flagging anything other than positive content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> LinkedIn solicits endorsements using <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> that generate skills members might have. Members cannot opt out of such solicitations, with the result that it sometimes appears that a member is soliciting an endorsement for a non-existent skill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing_platform">Publishing platform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Publishing platform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>LinkedIn continues to add different services to its platform to expand the ways that people use it. On May 7, 2015, LinkedIn added an analytics tool to its publishing platform. The tool allows authors to better track traffic that their posts receive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influencers">Influencers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Influencers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The LinkedIn Influencers program launched in October 2012 and features global <a href="/wiki/Thought_leader" title="Thought leader">thought leaders</a> who share their professional insights with LinkedIn's members. As of May 2016, there are 750+ Influencers, approximately 74% of which are male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The program is invite-only and features leaders from a range of industries including <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arianna_Huffington" title="Arianna Huffington">Arianna Huffington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_McKeown" title="Greg McKeown">Greg McKeown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martha_Stewart" title="Martha Stewart">Martha Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deepak_Chopra" title="Deepak Chopra">Deepak Chopra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Welch" title="Jack Welch">Jack Welch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_and_for-pay_research">Advertising and for-pay research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Advertising and for-pay research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In mid-2008, LinkedIn launched LinkedIn DirectAds as a form of sponsored advertising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In October 2008, LinkedIn revealed plans to open its social network of 30 million professionals globally as a potential sample for business-to-business research. It is testing a potential social network revenue model - research that to some appears more promising than advertising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> On July 23, 2013, LinkedIn announced their Sponsored Updates ad service. Individuals and companies can now pay a fee to have LinkedIn sponsor their content and spread it to their user base. This is a common way for social media sites such as LinkedIn to generate revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_plans">Future plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Future plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_graph">Economic graph</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economic graph">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Social_graph" title="Social graph">social graph</a>", LinkedIn CEO Jeff Weiner set a goal in 2012 to create an "economic graph" within a decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KovachBI_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-KovachBI-111">[111]</a></sup> The goal is to create a comprehensive digital map of the world economy and the connections within it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The economic graph was to be built on the company's current platform with data nodes including companies, jobs, skills, volunteer opportunities, educational institutions, and content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ForbesGraph_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesGraph-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> They have been hoping to include all the job listings in the world, all the skills required to get those jobs, all the professionals who could fill them, and all the companies (nonprofit and for-profit) at which they work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ForbesGraph_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesGraph-113">[113]</a></sup> The ultimate goal is to make the world economy and job market more efficient through increased transparency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KovachBI_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-KovachBI-111">[111]</a></sup> In June 2014, the company announced its "Galene" search architecture to give users access to the economic graph's data with more thorough filtering of data, via user searches like "Engineers with Hadoop experience in Brazil."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>LinkedIn has used economic graph data to research several topics on the job market, including popular destination cities of recent college graduates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> areas with high concentrations of technology skills,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and common career transitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> LinkedIn provided the City of New York with data from economic graph showing "in-demand" tech skills for the city's "Tech Talent Pipeline" project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dropped_features">Dropped features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Dropped features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In January 2013, LinkedIn dropped support for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LinkedIn_Answers" title="LinkedIn Answers">LinkedIn Answers</a>, and cited a new 'focus on development of new and more engaging ways to share and discuss professional topics across LinkedIn' as the reason for the retirement of the feature. The feature had been launched in 2007, and allowed users to post question to their network and allowed users to rank answers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_units">Business units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Business units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>LinkedIn derives its revenues from three business divisions:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Talent Solutions, through which recruiters and corporations pay for branded corporation and career listing pages, pay-per-click targeted job ads, and access to the LinkedIn database of users and resumes.</li>
<li>Marketing Solutions, which advertisers pay for pay per click-through targeted ads.</li>
<li>Premium Subscriptions, through which LinkedIn users can pay for advanced services, such as LinkedIn Business, LinkedIn Talent (for recruiters), LinkedIn JobSeeker, and LinkedIn Sales for sales professions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some elements of the various subscription services are also on a pay per use basis like InMail.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>LinkedIn has been described by online <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_publication" title="Trade publication">trade publication</a> <i><a href="/wiki/TechRepublic" title="TechRepublic">TechRepublic</a></i> as having "become the de facto tool for professional networking".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> LinkedIn has also been praised for its usefulness in fostering business relationships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> "LinkedIn is, far and away, the most advantageous social networking tool available to job seekers and business professionals today," according to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> LinkedIn has also received criticism, primarily regarding e-mail address mining and auto-update.</p>
<ul>
<li>The sign up process includes a step for entering your email password (there is an opt-out feature). LinkedIn will then offer to send out contact invitations to all members in your address book or that you have had email conversation with. When the member's email address book is opened it is opened with all email addresses selected and the member is advised invitations will be sent to "selected" email addresses, or to all. Up to 1500 invitations can then be sent out in one click, with no possibility to undo or withdraw them. LinkedIn was sued for sending out another two follow-up invitations to each contact from members to link to friends who had ignored the initial, authorized, invitation. In November 2014, LinkedIn lost a motion to dismiss the lawsuit, in a ruling that the invitations were advertisements not broadly protected by free speech rights that would otherwise permit use of people's names and images without authorization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The lawsuit was eventually settled in 2015 in favor of LinkedIn members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>Changing the description below a member's name is seen as a change in a job title, even if it is just a wording change or even a change to "unemployed". Unless a member opts to "turn off activity updates", an update is sent to all of that person's contacts, telling them to congratulate the member on the "new job".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>The feature that allows LinkedIn members to "endorse" each other's skills and experience has been criticized as meaningless, since the endorsements are not necessarily accurate or given by people who have familiarity with the member's skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan language</a> advocacy organization <a href="/wiki/Fundaci%C3%B3_puntCat" title="Fundació puntCat">Fundació puntCat</a> launched an online campaign asking LinkedIn to support the language both in the platform's interface and as CV language; it gained more than 3000 online signatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Plataforma_per_la_Llengua" title="Plataforma per la Llengua">Plataforma per la Llengua</a> started another campaign asking for such a change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_restrictions">International restrictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International restrictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_Syria" title="Internet censorship in Syria">Syrian</a> users reported that LinkedIn server stopped accepting connections originating from <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP addresses</a> assigned to Syria. The company's customer support stated that services provided by them are subject to US export and re-export control laws and regulations and "As such, and as a matter of corporate policy, we do not allow member accounts or access to our site from Cuba, Iran, North Korea, Sudan, or Syria."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2011, it was reported that LinkedIn was being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Internet censorship in the People's Republic of China">blocked in China</a> after calls for a "<a href="/wiki/2011_Chinese_pro-democracy_protests" title="2011 Chinese pro-democracy protests">Jasmine Revolution</a>". It was speculated to have been blocked because it is an easy way for dissidents to access <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, which had been <a href="/wiki/Censorship_of_Twitter" title="Censorship of Twitter">blocked</a> previously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> After a day of being blocked, LinkedIn access was restored in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2014, LinkedIn launched its Simplified Chinese language version named "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%A2%86" title="wikt:领">领</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%8B%B1" title="wikt:英">英</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Lǐngyīng</span></i>; literally: "leading elite"), officially extending their service in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters140225_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters140225-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> LinkedIn CEO Jeff Weiner acknowledged in a blog post that they would have to censor some of the content that users post on its website in order to comply with Chinese rules, but he also said the benefits of providing its online service to people in China outweighed those concerns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters140225_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters140225-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 August 2016, a Moscow court ruled that LinkedIn must be blocked in Russia for violating a new <a href="/wiki/Data_retention" title="Data retention">data retention</a> law, which requires the user data of Russian citizens to be stored on servers within the country. This ban was upheld on 10 November 2016, and all Russian ISPs began blocking LinkedIn thereafter. LinkedIn's mobile app was also banned from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Play_Store" title="Google Play Store">Google Play Store</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOS_App_Store" title="IOS App Store">iOS App Store</a> in Russia in January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-linkedinapprus_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-verge-linkedinapprus-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moscowtimes-upheld_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-moscowtimes-upheld-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="SNA_LinkedIn">SNA LinkedIn</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: SNA LinkedIn">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Search, Network, and Analytics (SNA) team at LinkedIn has a web site<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> that hosts the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> projects built by the group. Notable among these projects is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Voldemort" title="Project Voldemort">Project Voldemort</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Distributed_computing" title="Distributed computing">distributed</a> key-value <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Structured_storage" title="Structured storage">structured storage</a> system with low-<a href="/wiki/Latency_(engineering)" title="Latency (engineering)">latency</a> similar in purpose to Amazon.com's <a href="/wiki/Dynamo_(storage_system)" title="Dynamo (storage system)">Dynamo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BigTable" title="BigTable">BigTable</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Surveillance_and_NSA_program">Surveillance and NSA program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=LinkedIn&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Surveillance and NSA program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_global_surveillance_disclosures" title="2013 global surveillance disclosures">2013 global surveillance disclosures</a>, documents released by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> revealed that British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GCHQ" title="GCHQ">GCHQ</a> infiltrated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgacom" title="Belgacom">Belgacom</a> network by luring employees to a false LinkedIn page.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20111026060901/http://www.translatemedia.com/news/LinkedIn-Launches-in-Japan~800616257.html" rel="nofollow">"LinkedIn launches in Japan"</a>.
